  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dc363010-b0f7-4813-8d9c-6930170600f6'
      });
    }

<div id="review_1656012976" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1656012976" />
    <a title="Dolly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019021-dolly"><img alt="Dolly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1223325529p2/1019021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656012976?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dolly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dolly" href="/user/show/1019021-dolly">Dolly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060269876" href="/book/show/1429433.Chasing_Redbird">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">middle grade readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=read-but-not-finished-reviewing">read-but-not-finished-reviewing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=other-usa">other-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=gardens-flowers">gardens-flowers</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=pets">pets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=lorton-jammin-book-party">lorton-jammin-book-party</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656012976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1089025237573875505">Our local library children's book club selected this book for their June 2016 discussion. It's a fast read and really grabs at the reader's heart strings. <br/><br/>I liked that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11633.Sharon_Creech' title='Sharon Creech' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sharon Creech</a> weaves familiar names and places from other stories like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53496.Walk_Two_Moons' title='Walk Two Moons by Sharon Creech' rel='nofollow noopener'>Walk Two Moons</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19417.Absolutely_Normal_Chaos' title='Absolutely Normal Chaos by Sharon Creech' rel='nofollow noopener'>Absolutely Normal Chaos</a>. <br/><br/>The tale is sweet, yet melancholy. It is filled with longing and remembrance and even the hurt from missing our loved ones. But it also really shows how we all need some solitude at times and that the quiet can help s</span>
  <span id="freeText1089025237573875505" style="display:none">Our local library children's book club selected this book for their June 2016 discussion. It's a fast read and really grabs at the reader's heart strings. <br /><br />I liked that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11633.Sharon_Creech" title="Sharon Creech" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharon Creech</a> weaves familiar names and places from other stories like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/53496.Walk_Two_Moons" title="Walk Two Moons by Sharon Creech" rel="nofollow noopener">Walk Two Moons</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19417.Absolutely_Normal_Chaos" title="Absolutely Normal Chaos by Sharon Creech" rel="nofollow noopener">Absolutely Normal Chaos</a>. <br /><br />The tale is sweet, yet melancholy. It is filled with longing and remembrance and even the hurt from missing our loved ones. But it also really shows how we all need some solitude at times and that the quiet can help show us what is important in our lives. <br /><br />There is a mystical nature to the story, a sense that those who have passed are watching over us. And that in death, we are reunited with the loved ones who have passed before us. <br /><br />It's a nice sentiment and brings comfort to the characters in the story. But I find it interesting that it is only the oldest and the youngest who truly embrace these thoughts. The rest are merely caught up in life. <br /><br />Overall, it's a fast and engaging read; I took longer than I expected to finish it, but I was only able to carve out short periods to read it. I like that it forced me to savor the story and really think about the ways in which the characters are connected. I find it amusing that Zinny has to leave on her adventure in order for her family to really take notice of her.<br /><br />interesting quotes:<br /><br /><i>"It was just that there didn't seem to be a lot to say that someone wasn't already saying. I liked listening."</i> (p. 7)<br /><br /><i>"At home, I'd skulk around, trying not to be noticed, and yet hoping, wishing, praying to be noticed."</i> (p. 48)<br /><br /><i>"Soon I noticed the white specks of stars, but still they weren't draped on a black sky, still it wasn't dark. And although I watched intently, I did not see the moment of dark, and I wondered if maybe it wasn't a moment at all."</i> (p. 157)<br /><br /><i>"I was always in a muddle about time. It didn't seem like a series of days, but one stretch of time, with light and dark blending into each other. Time went on and on; it didn't start and stop, as I had thought. If time didn't start and stop, I thought, maybe life didn't either. Maybe it just went on and on."</i> (p. 164)<br /><br /><i>"'Til Next We Meet."</i> (p. 232)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1089025237573875505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2021209998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021209998" />
    <a title="Ashley Jacobson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17846660-ashley-jacobson"><img alt="Ashley Jacobson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530340775p2/17846660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021209998?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Jacobson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Jacobson" href="/user/show/17846660-ashley-jacobson">Ashley Jacobson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17846660-ashley-jacobson?shelf=read-youth">read-youth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021209998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18022053803152154360">What? I'm surprised that this is the same author as Walk Two Moons....well I guess I'm not surprised, but the difference in quality could not be any different! It's another quirky girl finding herself after a loved one leaves her life. But this book was just odd! I don't even want my kids reading it. The plot was weird and the lessons were not what I want my kids reading.<br/><br/>The aunt and the whole drawer thing is off, but it's even worse that she kept her dead baby in one. And then the creepy shrine</span>
  <span id="freeText18022053803152154360" style="display:none">What? I'm surprised that this is the same author as Walk Two Moons....well I guess I'm not surprised, but the difference in quality could not be any different! It's another quirky girl finding herself after a loved one leaves her life. But this book was just odd! I don't even want my kids reading it. The plot was weird and the lessons were not what I want my kids reading.<br /><br />The aunt and the whole drawer thing is off, but it's even worse that she kept her dead baby in one. And then the creepy shrine and dolls and world that they ran away to. What? I can look past the young girl spending 10 days at a time alone in the wilderness, especially since dad flies by to check up on her, but that long with the rest of the book is a turn off. <br /><br />Don't even get me started on the stalker, creepy older boy! Seriously? This is not ok. Boys, DO NOT take a page out of this kid's books! This is not how you get a girl. When she says no, it means no. I tend to think people go overboard on the no means no idea, but this is just one big N-O! Get a clue and stop being a creep! And then the stealing? Huh? This is portrayed as not ok, but it was still glorified. And Zinny wanted him to steal a horse because she was so desperate. Kids should not be in situations like that! <br /><br />And then Zinny is ok with his actions. Not at first, but then she becomes more and more ok. And super ok by the end. No! Why is this ok to portray?<br /><br />I could go on and on. Things that don't usually bug me did in this book because she much was off. Like how Zinny didn't feel like she belonged in her family, which is big and loud. Her parents don't try to help. They just let her go out on an odd trail on her own and check in every 10 days. Yes please, child. Leave and be gone for weeks and only check in for a bit. I think this is a great way to help you feel more loved and accepted. And why do big families have to be so chaotic? I don't have a big family. I didn't come from a big family. But I'm offended that they have to be portrayed this way.<br /><br />Anyways....overall I don't want my kids to read this because of the morals it seems to preach. Theft, creepy ways to deal with dead people, stalking, not standing up for yourself, leaving your family, not healthy self discovery, not healthy coping skills, and so much more. Just wow. Super shocked and sad!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18022053803152154360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer996239972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5391718529023039529">With profound insight, Sharon Creech reminds all of us how insular our world is as a child. Twelve year old Zinny spends the summer uncovering a path she found that leads from her farm to the shores of the Ohio River. With each foot of dirt and weeds she pushes away she gains insights into her family she had always taken for granted and understands that many of her childhood assumptions are untrue. Zinny assumes her words and actions affect the huge life issues she witnesses throughout her child</span>
  <span id="freeText5391718529023039529" style="display:none">With profound insight, Sharon Creech reminds all of us how insular our world is as a child. Twelve year old Zinny spends the summer uncovering a path she found that leads from her farm to the shores of the Ohio River. With each foot of dirt and weeds she pushes away she gains insights into her family she had always taken for granted and understands that many of her childhood assumptions are untrue. Zinny assumes her words and actions affect the huge life issues she witnesses throughout her childhood. In "Chasing Redbird" we witness Zinny's world grow to encompass sorrow, beauty, grief, and happiness in which she is not in control. Even though I found myself rushing to find out what secret or mystery was going to be uncovered next, I hated for the book to end. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813664-peter-heinrich?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622115262" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11572957542764045069">Creech knows how to tell the story of someone coming to terms with family, self, and painful (often devastating) loss. The details are always interesting along the way, and the writing clear and un-self-conscious.<br/><br/>I did have a little trouble with this book, though, because of the whole Rose component of the story. By "trouble" I mean I'm a pushover for that kind of thing and can easily be manipulated into any emotional corner desired. Was I a mess when we discover what's stored at the cabin? Big </span>
  <span id="freeText11572957542764045069" style="display:none">Creech knows how to tell the story of someone coming to terms with family, self, and painful (often devastating) loss. The details are always interesting along the way, and the writing clear and un-self-conscious.<br /><br />I did have a little trouble with this book, though, because of the whole Rose component of the story. By "trouble" I mean I'm a pushover for that kind of thing and can easily be manipulated into any emotional corner desired. Was I a mess when we discover what's stored at the cabin? Big deal. Lots of grown men get a little verklempt reading young-adult fiction.<br /><br />Seriously. I'm pretty sure I can't be the only one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14951637957442119123">I always know I'll like Sharon Creech's books.   <span id="freeText14951637957442119123" style="display:none">I always know I'll like Sharon Creech's books. I'd recently read Walk Two Moons and yesterday I needed a new middle grade to read so I grabbed Chasing Redbird off my daughter's shelf. And I had no idea it was a companion book to Walk Two Moons. I was even more enchanted by Zinnia Taylor and her family than I was by Sal and the Hiddles. <br /><br />Zinnia is lost in her big family. She hides in plain sight by being "the quiet one." She has always found solace with her beloved Aunt Jessie and Uncle Nate who live in an adjoining home. But now Aunt Jessie is gone and Uncle Nate seems to be losing it, so Zinny needs something else. She finds the beginning of an old overgrown trail near their property and begins clearing it, discovering in the process that it's the remains of a trail that once went twenty miles from her town of Bybanks to nearby Chocton. She devotes herself to clearing the entire length of the trail, and meanwhile finds herself drawn to the sweet attentions of Jake Boone, who has newly returned to Bybanks.<br /><br />Simply an enchanting story. I couldn't put it down. Sharon Creech is nothing but a dad-blasted treasure!</span>

<div id="review_48644076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48644076" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1441652-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1221054989p2/1441652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48644076?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/1441652-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1441652-wendy?shelf=q32009">q32009</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48644076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13881265224775086085">Chasing Redbird is written by Sharon Creech, and is about thirteen-year old Zinny Taylor who lives in Kansas on her families farm. She grows up with her two older brothers and her Aunt "Redbird" and Uncle Nate. She grows up becoming best friends with her cousin Rose all her childhood until she suddenly dies, of whooping cough at a young age. Zinny spends almost every second she can trying to find a way to get away from her family and the seldom privacy of her small rural town, where everybody kn</span>
  <span id="freeText13881265224775086085" style="display:none">Chasing Redbird is written by Sharon Creech, and is about thirteen-year old Zinny Taylor who lives in Kansas on her families farm. She grows up with her two older brothers and her Aunt "Redbird" and Uncle Nate. She grows up becoming best friends with her cousin Rose all her childhood until she suddenly dies, of whooping cough at a young age. Zinny spends almost every second she can trying to find a way to get away from her family and the seldom privacy of her small rural town, where everybody knows everybody. When her aunt dies and everything seems like it is falling apart, she takes on a load of guilt thinking that she was the reason for Rose's death and also the reason for her aunt's death. She finds a small trail in the near by woods on her family farm. When she just wants to be alone she finds that camping in the woods is one of the best places to be. As she makes a small place of her own in the woods she figures out many life problems and how to handle them. As her uncle Nate is having delusions about his dead wife, Zinny tries as hard as she can to help him make it through the pain. As she tries to find faith and love in just her simple place in the woods and simple family, she learns that sometimes it is not easy to find your place or reason in life but it all will work out if you just believe in yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13881265224775086085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_173269348" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173269348" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1711150-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1229139365p2/1711150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173269348?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/1711150-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1711150-catherine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173269348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12684284053047354788">If I could, I would give this book 2 1/2 starts. I'm not sure if I liked it or not. I didn't really like the characters. I found Zinny was selfish in many ways. I understand that she was dealing with grief, but the whole thing seemed really contrived. <br/><br/>I didn't like Jake, and I wouldn't want my daughter to date him - ever. He is dishonest, but then again, so is Zinny. I didn't like that Zinny was friends with Sal. That part bugged me. I loved Walk Two Moons, and I didn't want Zinny interloping on</span>
  <span id="freeText12684284053047354788" style="display:none">If I could, I would give this book 2 1/2 starts. I'm not sure if I liked it or not. I didn't really like the characters. I found Zinny was selfish in many ways. I understand that she was dealing with grief, but the whole thing seemed really contrived. <br /><br />I didn't like Jake, and I wouldn't want my daughter to date him - ever. He is dishonest, but then again, so is Zinny. I didn't like that Zinny was friends with Sal. That part bugged me. I loved Walk Two Moons, and I didn't want Zinny interloping on Sal's story. I thought the parents were poorly written. I don't for a minute believe parents would let a young girl spend 10 days out in the woods by herself - especially since there were bobcats, foxes, bears, and drunk hunters lurking about. All of the characters has severe communication problems/issues. This family was in need of theraphy - desperately!<br /><br />There are parts of this book that are beautifully written. I cried when I read about the plastic roses. I felt bad for Zinny when she painted a rose on her shirt instead of a zinnia. I liked how Creech let us see Zinny's confusion about herself and Rose. I also liked that her father flew overhead while she was out on the trail. I liked that Uncle Nathan helped the turtle find a mate. <br /><br />This book is worth reading, but it isn't as good as I expect from Creech. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12684284053047354788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2196472303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2196472303" />
    <a title="Sena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22879209-sena"><img alt="Sena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375819636p2/22879209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2196472303?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sena" href="/user/show/22879209-sena">Sena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22879209-sena?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22879209-sena?shelf=read-twice-or-more">read-twice-or-more</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196472303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13248323730726065810">When I was in the 5th grade, Sharon Creech was my favorite author. What I loved most about her was that she wrote <i>realistic</i> fiction (realistic enough for my 5th grade mind anyway.) She wrote about actual children, their families, and their feelings. <br/><br/>My love of Sharon Creech led me to Jerry Spinelli, who led me to Louis Sachar, who led me to Kate DiCamillo, and all these authors led me to become the person I am today. <br/><br/>With that being said, I was very nervous coming back to "Chasing Redbird". What</span>
  <span id="freeText13248323730726065810" style="display:none">When I was in the 5th grade, Sharon Creech was my favorite author. What I loved most about her was that she wrote <i>realistic</i> fiction (realistic enough for my 5th grade mind anyway.) She wrote about actual children, their families, and their feelings. <br /><br />My love of Sharon Creech led me to Jerry Spinelli, who led me to Louis Sachar, who led me to Kate DiCamillo, and all these authors led me to become the person I am today. <br /><br />With that being said, I was very nervous coming back to "Chasing Redbird". What if I felt that it was shallow or too childish to be entertaining for a twenty two year old? In the end, my fears were unneeded: 5th grader me had very good taste. <br /><br />"Chasing Redbird" focuses on grief and individuality. The thirteen year old protagonist Zinnia is stifled by her very large family, where everyone talks and talks but no one listens. The only person who made her feel special was her Aunt Jessie who died recently, leaving behind a heartbroken Uncle Nate. <br /><br /><blockquote>“Because I know who Zinny is. I know what she sounds like, smells like. I know what she radiates. I know who she <i>is.</i>”<br /><br />I wanted to ask <i>And who is that?,</i> but I didn’t.</blockquote><br /><br />When she finds an old abandoned trail starting in her backyard, she is determined to clear the trail and make it her own.<br /><br />The storyline is wonderful, with even a little bit of romance thrown in there (Jake Boone <i>must</i> have been my 5th grade crush at some point). The writing is filled with quaint little sayings that make the characters even more endearing. And through the character of Uncle Nate, we are actually shown a man who is so heartbroken with grief that he's "out of his noodle," and is having a very difficult time healing. It's a tough topic to tackle for a children's book, and yet. <br /><br />I also appreciate that Sharon Creech doesn't over-explain everyone's motivations, just because this is a children's book. Some things are left to the reader, for instance, we aren't really told whether Zinnia's mother felt resentment towards Aunt Jessie, or whether she was upset. This is hinted at, especially when Zinnia encounters a mother bear in the woods. However, we are never really <i>told,</i> we aren't shown a conversation between Zinnia and her mother about this. It is precisely this non-condescending attitude toward the intended audience that makes this book a good read for an adult as well. <br /><br />Now that I've confirmed that I still love Sharon Creech, I can go ahead and read some of her other works. Looking forward to it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13248323730726065810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2105308766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2105308766" />
    <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower"><img alt="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467816536p2/29402776.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2105308766?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower">The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9783596803033" href="/book/show/69495.Ich_Zinny_Taylor_">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2105308766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11789095593841774900"><b>5 stars!</b> <br/><br/><i>Ich, Zinny Taylor</i> has been a <b>fantastic read</b> - it actually had everything in order to get me hooked. <b>Zinny Taylor</b> and her six brothers and sisters are growing up on a farm in Kentucky and the <b>13-year-old teenager</b> is different from the other kids - she is <b>collecting a varity of things, is spending a lot of time outside of her family and is far from talkative</b>. When <b>Jake Boone</b> gets back to town and starts making Zinny a number of exciting gifts, she is sure that he is using her in order to </span>
  <span id="freeText11789095593841774900" style="display:none"><b>5 stars!</b> <br /><br /><i>Ich, Zinny Taylor</i> has been a <b>fantastic read</b> - it actually had everything in order to get me hooked. <b>Zinny Taylor</b> and her six brothers and sisters are growing up on a farm in Kentucky and the <b>13-year-old teenager</b> is different from the other kids - she is <b>collecting a varity of things, is spending a lot of time outside of her family and is far from talkative</b>. When <b>Jake Boone</b> gets back to town and starts making Zinny a number of exciting gifts, she is sure that he is using her in order to get closer to her older sister May - just like Tommy Salami and many other boys before. <br /><br />While the <b>blurb</b> of this story sound like a random coming-of-age story, the book is treating some very deep and emtional subjects and I felt incredibly close to the main characters of the story. <i>Ich, Zinny Taylor</i> is <b>heart-breaking, humerous and clever</b>. A perfect mixture!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11789095593841774900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2588399403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588399403" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60950857-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588399403?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/60950857-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588399403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16748162636297411258">I had to read this book in middle school and, not exaggerating at all, it emotionally traumatized me. I was in 6th grade so I was 11, and reading about Zinny feeling like she didn't belong and like everyone loved Rose more than her made me very, very upset. I remember several times trying not to cry in class while reading it; I don't know if it was legitimately abuse but it read like a story about neglect and child abuse. Then, finding the shrine, that's a traumatic happening to Zinny or any chi</span>
  <span id="freeText16748162636297411258" style="display:none">I had to read this book in middle school and, not exaggerating at all, it emotionally traumatized me. I was in 6th grade so I was 11, and reading about Zinny feeling like she didn't belong and like everyone loved Rose more than her made me very, very upset. I remember several times trying not to cry in class while reading it; I don't know if it was legitimately abuse but it read like a story about neglect and child abuse. Then, finding the shrine, that's a traumatic happening to Zinny or any child who'd find themself in that situation. It traumatized me an equal amount. A lot of stories/books I had to read in middle and high school (like The Dangerous Game, The Lottery, The Road, this one short story about WWII about how a zookeeper had to willingly let his pandas starve to death due to rations?????? I was bawling.) were really upsetting to me and I refrained from telling my parents about the material AND how much it upset me because I didn't want to upset them.<br /><br />I'm going to assume the reason why it was taught at my middle school was to help us open up our emotional capacity and understand things like feeling like an outsider in your family, grief, and how even adults struggle with grieving in a healthy way. Those are... valid lessons to teach children, but can be given without extreme examples that psychologically harm them. My father died when I was 4 so not only do I not need lessons on dealing with a fucked up family and grief, but reading stories about it greatly upset me. <br /><br />I also read a short-story in a textbook about a boy with a little brother who had a disability, who the older boy viewed as a burden. He wanted to go swimming but he brought his brother with him in a red wheelbarrow. A lightning storm came and his brother got electrocuted to death. The older brother has to bring his dead brother home in the red wheelbarrow to tell their mom what he did. Like, what the fuck? Why choose the most emotionally traumatizing examples to show kids to respect and be kind to each other, follow rules because people can get hurt, etc.? Why?<br /><br />I am almost 21 years old, and every so often these stories pop up in my brain and I wonder what the names were and why my schools chose to force us to read them. I describe them to my mother and she is horrified, telling me that as a grown adult in her 50's the topics are upsetting to her. I had to read The Road and I straight up could not describe what happens in that book because she'd be just as haunted as I am. <br /><br />I've finally found the name of the book with the familial neglect and traumatizing shrine of a corpse and the cousin named Rose everyone liked better. As a student who had to be taught with this material: it's not good for children. Lessons about growing up and dealing with grief can be handled better, without psychologically damaging the students. I discussed this with a friend and she said, "There's no way I could've read this at 11 without getting nightmares."</span>
  <a data-text-id="16748162636297411258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1536871060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1536871060" />
    <a title="Stacey Kym" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30580561-stacey-kym"><img alt="Stacey Kym" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452641818p2/30580561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1536871060?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey Kym" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey Kym" href="/user/show/30580561-stacey-kym">Stacey Kym</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/28930681-chasing-redbird">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30580561-stacey-kym?shelf=2016-reviews">2016-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1536871060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13152303845852965814">I only picked up 'Chasing Redbird' because it was short but let me tell you that I did not regret it! When it first started, I thought it was yet another "soulful" and "depressing" novel about yet another girl experiencing hard life and whining about it because she couldn't deal with it. Read it and done that. But, no...'Chasing Redbird' surprised me in a lot of ways. <br/>1) It grew on me.<br/>2) It intrigued me and made me actually want to read it.<br/>3) I totally understood the character.<br/>4) It made me cry.</span>
  <span id="freeText13152303845852965814" style="display:none">I only picked up 'Chasing Redbird' because it was short but let me tell you that I did not regret it! When it first started, I thought it was yet another "soulful" and "depressing" novel about yet another girl experiencing hard life and whining about it because she couldn't deal with it. Read it and done that. But, no...'Chasing Redbird' surprised me in a lot of ways. <br />1) It grew on me.<br />2) It intrigued me and made me actually want to read it.<br />3) I totally understood the character.<br />4) It made me cry.<br />5) Oh, and did I mention that I TOTALLY SHIPPED Zinny + Jake?<br />Congratulations to Sharon Creech on writing such a beautiful story of heartbreak, loss and healing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13152303845852965814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_59951643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59951643" />
    <a title="Mommalibrarian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/153169-mommalibrarian"><img alt="Mommalibrarian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199217249p2/153169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/59951643?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mommalibrarian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mommalibrarian" href="/user/show/153169-mommalibrarian">Mommalibrarian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/153169-mommalibrarian?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer59951643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6064203932283088472">The young teen, Zinnie, is definitely not perfect. She has no magic powers. The author bravely lets her make multiple mistakes which is good. It keeps the story interesting. The less than wonderful things in this book are the writer's devices: an excess of folky words and sayings that were so totally foreign as to seem made-up and worst of all reference to spaghetti and meatballs multiple places in the text as a binding device. All mentions were real stretches and took away from the narrative.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kW4D9H5+XCfV831MMdp2+4cMT+NzOrOI0Z/uAy56Ix/xf33ZZjxm5kynMPx6zCkfVxvhcyqkEVii7V35ENBE4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('usl2VfEOvyUkV+bqRC6NiQYsN0rtV8v9PIehfdcEse3a2Ah46UyF5L0Dq1oPONJt1juZ2rTJaS1P9RKH6a7WEQ==')})
  }

He is a great help around the house, and everybody except Snowbell the cat likes him a great deal. In spite of his small size, Stuart gets around in the world, riding a Fifth Avenue bus, racing (and winning in) a sailboat in Central Park, teaching school for a day, and so on. His size -- just over two inches -- does give him some trouble now and then, like the time he was rolled up in the window shade, or when he got dumped into a garbage scow. It is on this search that we leave Stuart, going north in his little car, sure he is heading in the right direction.   In this special gift-book edition of a beloved classic, renowned artist Rosemary Wells has lovingly added delicate watercolor to the original black-and-white drawings by Garth Williams.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11633.Sharon_Creech">About Sharon Creech</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/11633.Sharon_Creech"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1595481856p3/11633.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/11633.Sharon_Creech">Sharon Creech
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,370
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15661286787037993670">	I was born in South Euclid, Ohio, a suburb of Cleveland, and grew up there with my noisy and rowdy family: my parents (Ann and Arvel), my sister (Sandy), and my three brothers (Dennis, Doug and Tom).<br/>For a fictional view of what it was like growing up in my family, see Absolutely Normal Chaos. (In that book, the brothers even have the same names as my own brothers.) Our house was not only full of </span>
  <span id="freeText15661286787037993670" style="display:none">	I was born in South Euclid, Ohio, a suburb of Cleveland, and grew up there with my noisy and rowdy family: my parents (Ann and Arvel), my sister (Sandy), and my three brothers (Dennis, Doug and Tom).<br />For a fictional view of what it was like growing up in my family, see Absolutely Normal Chaos. (In that book, the brothers even have the same names as my own brothers.) Our house was not only full of us Creeches, but also full of friends and visiting relatives.<br />In the summer, we usually took a trip, all of us piled in a car and heading out to Wisconsin or Michigan or, once, to Idaho. We must have been a very noisy bunch, and I'm not sure how our parents put up with being cooped up with us in the car for those trips. The five-day trip out to Idaho when I was twelve had a powerful effect on me: what a huge and amazing country! I had no idea then that thirty-some years later, I would recreate that trip in a book called Walk Two Moons.<br />One other place we often visited was Quincy, Kentucky, where my cousins lived (and still live) on a beautiful farm, with hills and trees and swimming hole and barn and hayloft. We were outside running in those hills all day long, and at night we'd gather on the porch where more stories would be told. I loved Quincy so much that it has found its way into many of my books--transformed into Bybanks, Kentucky. Bybanks appears in Walk Two Moons and Chasing Redbird and Bloomability. Bybanks also makes a brief appearance (by reference, but not by name) in The Wanderer.<br />When I was young, I wanted to be many things when I grew up: a painter, an ice skater, a singer, a teacher, and a reporter. It soon became apparent that I had little drawing talent, very limited tolerance for falling on ice, and absolutely no ability to stay on key while singing. I also soon learned that I would make a terrible reporter because when I didn't like the facts, I changed them. It was in college, when I took literature and writing courses, that I became intrigued by story-telling. Later, I was a teacher (high school English and writing) in England and in Switzerland. While teaching great literature, I learned so much about writing: about what makes a story interesting and about techniques of plot and characterization and point of view. I started out writing novels for adults: The Recital and Nickel Malley were both written and published while I was living in England (these books were published in England only and are now out of print.) But the next book was Absolutely Normal Chaos, and ever since that book I have written mainly about young people. Walk Two Moons was the first of my books to be published in America. When it received the Newbery Medal, no one was more surprised than I was. I'm still a little bit in shock.<br />After Walk Two Moons came Chasing Redbird, Pleasing the Ghost, Bloomability, The Wanderer, and Fishing in the Air. I hope to be writing stories for a long, long time.<br />I am married to Lyle Rigg, who is the headmaster of The Pennington School in Pennington, New Jersey, and have two grown children, Rob and Karin. Being with my family is what I enjoy most. The next-best thing is writing stories.<br /><br />© Sharon Creech</span>
  <a data-text-id="15661286787037993670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1945168-chasing-redbird">Quotes from Chasing Redbird</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Maybe it was the same with people: if you studied them,you'd see new and different things. But would you like what you saw? Did it depend on who was doing the looking?&rdquo;</span>
